Li Jingcong Denies Suspension of Eurasia Air Route 113

According to the Central News Agency, regarding the report in a certain Western newspaper that the Eurasia Aviation Company is seriously considering suspending the Eurasia air route, Li Jingcong, the general manager of the company, solemnly denied it to the Central News Agency reporter yesterday morning and said that although the Eurasia air route has been temporarily suspended due to the Xinjiang war, it is actively preparing for it at all times. The claim that it is seriously considering suspension is inaccurate. Li also said that the Soviet TASS news agency reported that a new government has been established in Kashgar, separating from China. The company has not yet received any telegrams, and the Eurasia air route takes Sun through Dihua and Tacheng, which are far from the reported Kashgar. Even if the TASS report is true, it will not hinder the Eurasia traffic. According to the reporter, Kashgar has two cities, Han and Hui. Hancheng is now Shule County, Xinjiang, and Huicheng is Shufu County. In 1860, according to the Russian treaty, a commercial port was opened in Huicheng, which was the most prosperous in the entire province. Shufu is located on the south bank of the Ulan Wusu River, and Yule is located on the north bank of the Yabuya River, near the Pamir Mountains.

The All-Zhejiang Public Association's Concern for Zhejiang Province's Opium Prohibition 114

Telegram to the Executive Yuan

Two Telegrams Sent Yesterday and the Day Before

The All-Zhejiang Public Association in Shanghai sent a telegram to the Executive Yuan regarding the opium prohibition case in Zhejiang Province, which reads: "To the esteemed President of the Executive Yuan of the Nanjing National Government, Wang: We have observed that since the Zhejiang Provincial Government promulgated the Provisional Regulations for Eradicating Drugs, it has been quite effective. Now we understand that the Central Government, due to the revision of the Opium Prohibition Law, has issued a general order to all provinces to abolish their individual regulations within a set time limit. The Zhejiang Provincial Government has already submitted a request for an extension until the end of the 22nd year of the Republic. However, although opium and drugs have been eradicated in Zhejiang Province, neighboring provinces are still in the process of prohibition. The impact of this situation may cause the opium problem in Zhejiang Province to reignite. In addition to the Zhejiang Provincial Government requesting an extension of the implementation period, our association believes that since these individual regulations have been effectively implemented in Zhejiang Province, if the Central Government is truly determined to prohibit opium, it should adopt the Zhejiang method and implement it in all provinces, intensifying the prohibition efforts. In this way, the opium prohibition in Zhejiang Province will not be affected, and there will be a day when the opium disaster in the whole country is eradicated. We humbly submit this report and respectfully request its adoption and implementation. The All-Zhejiang Public Association of Shanghai kowtows."

Telegram to the Zhejiang Provincial Government

The All-Zhejiang Public Association in Shanghai sent a telegram to the Zhejiang Provincial Government regarding the opium prohibition case in Zhejiang Province, which reads: "To the esteemed Chairman of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, Lu: At the seventh meeting of the board of directors of our association, it was proposed that your esteemed chairman consult on matters concerning opium prohibition in Zhejiang Province. After discussion, it was deemed necessary to continue extending the Provisional Regulations for Eradicating Drugs and to request the Central Government to adopt the Zhejiang method, implementing it in all provinces and intensifying the prohibition efforts, so that the opium prohibition in Zhejiang Province will not be affected by neighboring provinces. We have already telegraphed the Executive Yuan to adopt and implement this proposal. Furthermore, our association resolved at the end of last year to request a postponement of the dismissal of the opium prohibition committees in various counties. The purpose of this was that although opium prohibition in Zhejiang Province has shown promise, any relaxation would lead to a resurgence of the problem, repeating the mistakes of the third year of the Republic. If the opium prohibition committees continue to exist, they can still fulfill their responsibilities of guidance and supervision. Now that the Provisional Regulations for Eradicating Drugs have been extended, these opium prohibition committees should continue to operate accordingly. We hereby respectfully submit this request, hoping for your consideration. The All-Zhejiang Public Association of Shanghai kowtows."

Zhang Zishu Returns from Outside the Pass and Talks About the Various Measures Taken by the Japanese in Manchuria 115

Every Word is True

Letting Go of Management, In an Instant, the Land and People No Longer Belong to Us 116

Building Roads and Stone Forts to Defend Against Russia and Control the People's Militia

Seizing Land and Using Civilian Labor, Causing Extreme Hardship and Suffering

Engaging in Large-Scale Construction, Japanese Troops Spread Across the Land, Consolidating Their Territory

A Nominal Government Holds Power, While in War, They Become Sacrifices

Zhang Zishu, the Chief of Staff of the Second Army under Li Futing, formerly of the Jilin Self-Defense Army under Ding Chao, recently returned to Shanghai after conducting an on-site investigation of the situation in Northeast China. As Zhang Xueliang returns to the country from Europe, Representative Zhang brought the report and intended to visit Zhang to report everything. Because Zhang entered Beijing, they have not met. A reporter from the Guowen News Agency yesterday visited Chief of Staff Zhang at his residence, who provided a very detailed account of the situation of the Japanese army in the Northeast, as he had observed it during the past two months. Mr. Zhang said, "Since the fall of the Northeast, Japan, in its puppet state of Manchuria, has taken control of all aspects of politics, economy, border defense, finance, land, industry, commerce, real estate, and various construction projects. For the sake of clarity, I will present them in detail below."

Slogans Promoting Japanese-Manchurian Friendship

(1) The Japanese have posted slogans in the puppet state promoting the everlasting friendship between Japan and Manchuria, the stationing of Japanese troops in Manchuria to protect the government, and all management, construction, and building activities. (2) Stone forts are being built to guard bridges along the Harbin-Changchun Railway line. Four stone forts are being built on the south and north mountains of Yimianpo, and four stone forts are being built on the north and south mountains of Hengdaohezi. Five stone forts are being built at Hailin Station. More than ten stone forts are being built from Mijiang to Tielinghe, all for the purpose of defending against Russia.

Japanese Troops Deployed in Various Parts of Northern Manchuria

(3) Approximately two hundred Japanese troops are stationed in Yimianpo, and approximately one hundred Japanese troops are stationed in Hengdaohezi. About a brigade of Japanese troops is stationed at Hailin Station, Mishan Muling County, Bamiantong, and Tielinghe. The details for the Harbin-Manzhouli line are unknown. (4) Japanese troops are constructing facilities at the wharves and counties along the Songhua River downstream from Harbin to Sanchahe and the Wusuli River. In Harbin's Nangang, fourteen Japanese barracks, all two-story buildings, are being built in front of the Confucian Temple. Each building is sixty zhang long, with more than 120 rooms. The fourteen buildings have a total of more than 1,700 rooms. The airfield covers an area of over 4,000 mu, extending from the west of Jile Temple to Dongmajiagou and from east to Guxiangtun, spanning five li from east to west and four li from north to south, with more than 4,500 mu of land. 1,300 to 1,400 buildings are being constructed, along with thirteen large iron buildings, each nine zhang wide and long, capable of storing ten aircraft. There are two large iron buildings capable of storing twelve aircraft. Three lines of trenches, barbed wire, and electrified fences have been installed. More than 120 aircraft are stored there. Chinese workers are hired as laborers, with five to six hundred people working on construction every day. I worked there for four days, earning eight jiao per day. After paying for food, I had only four jiao left. Only then did I learn the true nature of the facilities. Dozens of Japanese pilots practiced flying every day, ascending to three to four thousand meters, performing flips and turns. The airfield and the pilot and maintenance personnel are permanently stationed by more than 2,000 soldiers. A division of Japanese troops is permanently stationed in Harbin. The first warehouse is at the Eighth Station in Harbin, and the second warehouse is in the Nili Factory south of the Qinjiagang Railway Station. Military equipment, uniforms, and supplies are piled up like mountains.

Building Railways for Military Purposes

(5) The Laha Railway Station is being built under the Wenmiao Kan of Jile Temple in Nangang, Binjiang County, about three or four li long. The section from Sanke Tree in the east of the county to Taga River in Acheng in the southeast is about thirty li east of the railway. The entire line is composed of Japanese streets, and Chinese people are not allowed to loiter there. Armed Japanese citizens are moving in, and construction is underway. (6) The Laji Road from Lalin Cang Street in Acheng County to Jilin City is connected to the Hulan-Hailun Railway via the Lalin Harbin Sanke Tree and the Laha Road. The seventeen spans of the Dajiang Railway Bridge have been completed and will soon be open to traffic. The previously built dirt roads were all constructed by recruiting workers. If there were one hundred households in a village, twenty people would be required to build dirt roads and perform various tasks with the Japanese, and each person would be paid one ocean dollar per day. The railway from Hailun to Heihe has already reached not far from Aigun and is not yet completed. The railway from Heihe, the provincial capital of Heilongjiang, to Nehe, is more than two hundred li long. Once completed, it will be open to traffic. (7) Japanese troops are building Yilan County in the southern bank of the lower reaches of the Songhua River, in Jilin Province, with approximately sixty to seventy soldiers. Six stone forts are being built, three along Xiaojiangzi and three east of the street. The airfield is not large and has not been greatly constructed. Approximately three to four hundred Japanese troops are stationed in Jiamusi, in Huachuan County. Eight stone forts are being built on the southern mountain, and three buildings are being built. More than ten li east of the street base below the mountain and six east-west streets are being constructed, about five li away from Jiamusi Street. The airfield has about forty mu of land, and the houses are made of wood and iron. Approximately one hundred and fifty Japanese troops are stationed in Fujin County Street, and there are frequent conflicts with our people's militias. The airfield has four to five hundred mu of land.

The Northeast Corner is a Clean Land

(8) No Japanese troops are stationed in the southeastern counties of Fujin County, such as Baoqing, Mishan, and Boli. Only our people's militias come and go. Japanese troops often go to Huachuan County, Jiamusi, and Fujin to engage in conflicts with our people's militias. No Japanese troops are stationed in the counties of Tongjiang, Raohe, and Hulin, from Sanchahe in the northeast to the Wusuli River. The flag of the Blue Sky with a White Sun is hung in Hulin and Raohe counties. The person in charge of Hulin County, Gao Yushan, has three to four thousand men under his command. (9) In the puppet state, the Japanese have the authority to completely search the homes of residents in the four eastern provinces for firearms of all sizes, which must be handed over to the districts, then to the counties, and finally to the Japanese advisory officials for inspection. Those who fail to hand over their firearms will be reported, and their entire family will be executed. The informant will receive a reward of fifty yuan, and the property will be confiscated. In Tangyuan County, Heilongjiang Province, north of the Songhua River, County Magistrate Liu and the Chief of the Internal Affairs Section were executed in the eighth month of the lunar calendar because the disaster relief clothing had not been distributed. The Japanese advisory official dispatched ten Japanese soldiers to the county government, tied up County Magistrate Liu and Chief of the Internal Affairs Section Xia, and executed them outside the government. First, a telegram was sent to Commander Guanglai in Harbin, and then a telegram was sent to Jiang Province.

Tears of Blood of the People of the Puppet State of XinJing

(11) The Japanese are building the puppet state of XinJing in Changchun, which is the new capital of Japan. Each side is thirty li long. Except for the old city, all are Japanese street bases. The Japanese occupied the area outside the west gate of the old city and completely moved our people to the east of the old city. They also built fifteen new streets and allocated land to industrial, commercial, and civilian residents, claiming it was in the west city. The money the Japanese paid for the land they occupied was not enough to buy land in the east city. The people are all crying and weeping, saying that being slaves to a conquered nation is truly unbearable. If they don't sell, they are forced to. They forcibly occupy the land, and they have to move. If they don't move, they forcibly demolish their houses. This is the treatment the people receive, and it is truly unbearable. (11) The Executive Government is in the southwest, but construction has not yet begun. Puyi used to live in a building on Qima Road but has now moved to a small room in the salt warehouse office on Liuma Road. The interior is guarded by the Japanese, with two floors, and the exterior is guarded by the Imperial Guard of the puppet state, with two-story guard posts. Movement is not free. The Japanese are building the headquarters of the Kwantung Governor-General, a seven-story building, all made of ceramic bricks and tiles, very sturdy. Opposite the Japanese station is a main road, about two li away from the station, on the west side of the road. It is better built than the Korean Governor-General's Office. To the north are four Japanese barracks, capable of housing two divisions, each occupying approximately four thousand mu of land, totaling over eighteen thousand mu. (12) There are two airfields. The northeastern airfield is approximately four thousand seven hundred mu, with more than 1,500 buildings and fourteen large iron buildings, each capable of storing ten aircraft. The airfield on the north side is slightly smaller, approximately four thousand mu, with over a thousand buildings and seven large iron buildings, storing the same number of aircraft as the other two, one hundred and eighty or ninety aircraft. The airfield is staffed by approximately four thousand pilots, maintenance personnel, and guards. Several lines of tunnels and electrified fences have been constructed, with very strict security. To build the airfields, over a thousand Chinese laborers are working at both locations. The main streets opposite the train station all have large squares marked with standards. The Chinese laborers working in Changchun earn eight jiao per day, with three to four ten thousand.

The Puppet State's Currency is Managed by the Japanese

(13) In terms of the economy, in June of the third year of the puppet state, an announcement was issued to all provinces that all miscellaneous currencies would be abolished and that all miscellaneous tickets would be exchanged for puppet state currency as soon as possible. Next year, everything will be converted to puppet state currency. The Japanese military's salaries and needs in the puppet state are paid as follows: general officers receive 2,600-2,800 yuan per month, field grade officers receive 1,600-1,800 yuan, junior officers receive 500-800 yuan, and enlisted men and servants receive 50-90 yuan. All expenses are paid by the puppet state bank, and salaries are paid on the 25th of each month. The Japanese say that since they are helping Manchuria fight, all revenue from customs and duties is managed by the Japanese. (14) The Japanese-Korean Rice Field Joint-Stock Company is established in Abin County and other places, purchasing land adjacent to the river from the people. Land worth three hundred yuan is given one hundred yuan. One qing is ten mu. Land of medium quality is given fifty yuan for ten mu. Land with trees, fodder, and wasteland is given a price of twenty or ten yuan, or less. If they don't sell, they are forcibly assessed. (15) The Japanese military calculates that they have small conflicts with the Northeastern People's Army every day. Every day, people from the four eastern provinces and Inner Mongols enter the pass. The puppet state has established the Xin'an Province, where there are also many people's militias who often resist the Japanese military. (16) High-altitude telegraphs are installed along the South Manchuria Railway line, from Lushunkou, Dalian, Korea, Andong, Fushun, and Ji Hui. The routes all have large iron frames and high-altitude currents. The railways are all double-tracked. Slogans are posted at each station and town: "Japanese-Manchurian Friendship and Joint Rule."

Japanese Education Destroys People's Knowledge

(17) Education focuses on the Japanese language. Currently, the first and second middle schools in the Harbin Special District have been abolished, and two middle schools in the new puppet state of XinJing have been abolished. Gradually, all middle schools will be abolished, leaving only high primary schools. People are required to study old Confucian books to qualify, and scientific books are used less. This is to destroy people's knowledge so that later generations of young people will not have knowledge. (18) The Japanese are managing the mining industry, actively developing all mining operations, including gold, silver, copper, iron, tin, and lead. The French also want to invest, but no agreement has been reached. Two gold factories have been established, one in Huapi Gou in Hualdian County, Jilin Province, and one in Baisha River, Dongning County. Both places produce very good gold. This is the mining industry in operation. The Donglaoye Ridge glass mine in Yanshou County has been inspected and will be developed. A large woolen mill has been established in Harbin and is currently under construction at the Nitong Railway Station. (19) The Japanese have arrested more than twenty people from the Chinese Eastern Railway, including Russian officials. The Russian consul and railway director have all returned to their country. Japan and Russia are actively preparing for war, and Japanese military supplies are piled up like mountains.

Eliminating the Old and Reducing the New to Prepare for the Enemy Russia

(20) The Japanese are planning to eliminate the old army of the puppet state and increase the new army, starting with Liaoning. Each county police district will have thirty men, aged eighteen to forty, trained by the Japanese to prepare for the enemy Russia. Therefore, the people are panicked. The people of the Northeast are crying out to the heavens and earth. In the future, the people of the Northeast provinces will shed rivers of blood, and their white bones will face the sky. The Japanese have informed all counties in Jilin and the Northeast to prepare more than three thousand large carts for war use. (21) The harvest in the four northeastern provinces is very good. The Japanese have issued an order to quickly harvest the rice and actively push rice, storing it in grass bags. Mung beans are seven or eight yuan per shi, with a weight of four or five hundred jin per shi. Red sorghum rice is four jiao per dou, with no market. The wages for plowing and hoeing in the spring are very high. The Japanese have notified the counties to urge the collection of rents and taxes, and various official fees are still collected by the puppet state, which must be paid quickly. The farmers work hard all year, and the harvested grain is not enough to spend, and the people's livelihood is truly unsustainable, and so on.

Unite to Promote National Products

All members of the nation and ethnic group should strive to promote national products, and especially to practice what they preach, because promoting national products can save the bankruptcy of the countryside, the decline of industry and commerce, the exhaustion of finance, and the danger of the nation and ethnic group. Taking agriculture as an example, promoting national products can resist the dumping of food by imperialists, increase the price of our agricultural products, and sell them well in various places, so as to increase the income of farmers, improve the livelihood of farmers, and establish the foundation of our national economy. Taking commerce as an example, promoting national products can eliminate the current unbalanced phenomenon, completely stop the shameful behavior of traitorous merchants buying and selling for foreigners to extract the cream of compatriots, and make Chinese merchants all become members of promoting social production. Taking national finance as an example, promoting national products can fully develop agriculture, industry, and commerce, and national finance will inevitably tend to stability, and national income can be drastically increased. With the country rich and the domestic power sufficient, all construction of the country can be actively promoted in order to seek economic independence of the country. Therefore, promoting national products is necessary in all aspects. To put it more clearly, promoting national products is the only way to love and save the country, to defeat the economic aggression of the imperialists, and the only force for the Chinese nation to fight for survival. May all compatriots unite to promote national products, and everyone practice what they preach. "Everyone works hard, promotes national products, and uses national products." China's Trade with Spain 118

Decreased Last Year Compared to Previous Years

According to the news released by the Guidance Department of the International Trade Bureau yesterday, China's exports to Spain have always been dominated by the silk industry and porcelain, while imports have been mostly machinery, vehicles, chemicals, paper, alcohol, etc. However, in recent years, China's export goods have failed to improve and compete with others, so the export volume has been far less than in the past. According to the investigation, Spain's total imports in 1932 were worth 925,72,628 gold pesetas, and China's imports were 2,876,193 gold pesetas (each gold peseta is approximately equal to one Chinese yuan), accounting for only 3/1000 of the total imports, ranking 40th among the trade positions of various countries. The commercial relations between China and Spain have not been fully developed. China was once famous in the world for its silk, tea, and porcelain, but in recent years, it has plummeted. Taking Spain as an example, in 1932, the total value of imported silk fabrics was 24,877,878 gold pesetas, of which Italy accounted for 13,116,177, France accounted for 4,916,567, Germany accounted for 300,841, Switzerland accounted for 1,287,562, the Netherlands accounted for 849,446, Belgium accounted for 499,667, and China only imported 144,406 gold pesetas, which is vastly different from other countries. In terms of porcelain, in 1932, Spain's total import value was 749,775, of which Germany accounted for 419,575, Czechoslovakia accounted for 133,647, Japan accounted for 91,867, and China only imported 5,991 gold pesetas. In terms of tea, in 1932, Spain imported 394,887 gold pesetas, of which British India imported 317,917, and China only 70,543. China was once a major exporter of silk, tea, and porcelain, but now it is far behind others. Although the reasons are not one-sided, China's production technology does need to be improved: (1) The reduction of production costs must be rationalized. (2) The decoration must be beautiful. (3) The materials must be clean, so that China can have hope of restoring its international trade.

Special Dredger Ordered from Germany 119

Will Arrive in Early Spring Next Year

To Dredge the Silt at the Mouth of the River

The North China Daily News reported that the 40 million tons of silt at the mouth of the Yangtze River, and how to dredge it to make the river mouth 9 feet deep so that large ships can enter and exit, has long been a difficult problem. Recently, the Huangpu Conservancy Bureau has ordered a special dredger from Germany, so this problem can be solved. The price is approximately 2.35 million yuan at the current exchange rate. It is not yet possible to determine how long it will take to dredge all the silt. The machine will arrive in early spring next year and will begin work immediately. The proposal to deepen the waterway at the mouth of the Yangtze River was first proposed about 60 years ago, but it was shelved due to the scale of the project. In recent years, Huangpu Conservancy engineers, Dr. Chatley, repeatedly investigated the situation at the mouth of the river, prepared a report, and submitted it to the government, which was finally approved. The special dredger ordered is the result of years of research by the bureau. It can dredge three tons of mud every ten hours. Dr. Chatley told a representative of the North China Daily News that the Huangpu Conservancy Bureau has been considering the issue of deepening the waterway at the mouth of the Yangtze River for fourteen years. The heavy accumulation of silt at the mouth of the river is a major obstacle for ships with deeper drafts. In 1876, the former chief engineer, Mr. Trigick, advocated deepening the mouth of the river, but no one paid attention to it. It was not until 1915 that he jointly discussed this matter with the Jianghai Customs and made a special investigation. In 1920, Dr. Chatley prepared a report for Mr. Hedenstam, stating the possibility of deepening the mouth of the river with a suction dredger. This report was passed by the International Advisory Engineering Committee of the Shanghai Port Investigation Office the following year and submitted to the government. Finally, with the assistance of the chairman of the bureau, Song Ziwen, it was approved by the Executive Yuan in 1930. In 1933, bids were solicited for the construction of the first special dredger. There were ten bidders from various countries, and the German Shizhou Trading Company offered the lowest price and had special experience in manufacturing this type of machine, so it won the bid. The machine looks like a cargo ship, 360 feet long and 60 feet wide, with a draft of 18 feet when carrying 4,000 tons of mud. It can dredge 25,000 cubic yards of mud per day, or more than 30,000 tons of mud every ten hours. The dredged mud will be dumped into the sea two miles away. The Huangpu Conservancy Bureau has specially dispatched the dredging engineer of the bureau, Mr. Smith, and two Chinese mechanical engineers to Germany to supervise the construction. It is expected to be completed and shipped to Shanghai in early spring next year.

Public Concession Bureau Annual Health Report for Last Year 121

Chinese Suffer More Severe Stomach Ailments

More Attention Should Be Paid to Food Safety

The Acting Director of the Health Department of the Public Concession Bureau submitted a report to the Board of Directors on the work for the entire previous year, stating that the year was generally peaceful with no unexpected events. Except for a slight spread of influenza in July and August, there were very few other disasters.

Birth and Death Statistics: The birth rate of foreigners this year was 17.87 per thousand. This statistic is being published for the first time in this district, based on reports provided by doctors and hospitals, and is generally considered accurate. As for Chinese residents, many are still unaware of the importance of registration, and a considerable number of newborns, especially girls, are abandoned. Fewer births are attended by hospitals and doctors, so it is difficult to obtain accurate statistics at this time.

Number of Deaths: The death rate for foreigners was 11.29 per thousand. The reported death rate for Chinese was 12.82 per thousand (compared to 17.65 in the previous year). However, 42 percent of the deaths, or 5,715 cases, were unclaimed bodies. Therefore, this number for the Chinese is not suitable for comparison. If mandatory registration were implemented, there might be some improvement in the results. However, due to various customs, it is feared that the degree of inaccuracy would still not be easily corrected.

Infectious Diseases: This year, stomach ailments were more prevalent, and the reported number of Chinese sufferers increased significantly, with many deaths. This may be due to incomplete reporting or the particularly severe nature of the disease in this area. Furthermore, considering the prevalence of stomach ailments, more attention should be paid to food safety. Although the Health Department has made every effort to ensure food safety, residents should not therefore neglect to take their own precautions. No cases of cholera occurred this year, which is a rare occurrence in this city. This may be because the disease spread so widely last year that most people have now acquired immunity. In addition, the supply of water to the common people and the implementation of various vaccination methods have contributed to this success. Alternatively, it may be due to the cyclical nature of the disease, with this year being a period of dormancy. At this moment, it is not possible to determine definitively, but we cannot be optimistic about the coming year.

Hospital Issues: After the Board of Directors adopted the report of the Hospital Issues Investigation Committee, the Health Department formulated a construction plan for the Western District Fever Hospital, as recommended, and construction will begin as soon as a site is selected. The planned mental hospital will require further modifications after the plan has been drafted. Furthermore, regarding the request for subsidies by private hospitals, a framework will soon be established to define standards for the construction and equipment of hospitals seeking assistance, in order to ensure effectiveness and uniformity.

New Slaughterhouse: The Bureau's new slaughterhouse has been completed and gradually put into use in November and December. Slaughtering is performed entirely using the most humane methods. The waste meat disposal machine should be moved out of the slaughterhouse immediately, preferably to a location opposite. The new meat market and cold storage facilities are currently under construction. The Bureau-operated pig slaughterhouse is being planned for expansion, and it seems necessary to find a larger site to allow for full equipment. For the sake of public health and the Bureau's revenue, this business should be gradually expanded.

Milk Sterilization: Regarding the issue of mandatory sterilization of Grade B milk, a committee has been appointed by the Bureau to study the matter after it was presented by the Health Department, and the process is not yet complete. The sale of "white-collapse oil" and vegetable "white-collapse oil" has been subject to new licensing regulations, which limit the use of preservatives to two parts per thousand and also allow the use of non-toxic colorings.

School Inspections: All schools receiving subsidies are regularly inspected for cleanliness. At the end of the year, physical examinations were initiated on a trial basis at one Chinese primary school. The results are certain to be of great value.

Publicity Work: Because public health was good this year, some progress has been made in health education. Various new slogans and illustrations have been posted in the health sub-bureaus and on billboards in various locations, and the tram and bus companies have provided special assistance by posting advertisements on their vehicles.

Joint Announcement by Jianghai Customs 122

Tang Hai'an, Superintendent of Jianghai Customs, and Berlot, Customs Commissioner, yesterday jointly issued two announcements regarding the revised standards for classifying and taxing imported diesel and kerosene, as well as amendments to the regulations for general cargo warehouses. The announcements are as follows:

Revised Standards for Diesel and Kerosene Taxes: We have now received an order from the Ministry of Finance stating that, for imported diesel and kerosene with related properties, the following classifications are established as standards for taxation: (A) Diesel: Specific gravity at 20 degrees Celsius above 0.900 and flash point (according to the Cless method) above 95 degrees Celsius, taxed at 2.90 gold units per ton. (B) Other (including crude oil for extraction), taxed at 26.30 gold units per ton. Kerosene (including other mineral oils for ignition, with a specific gravity of 0.78 to 0.90) will be taxed at the same rate as before. We are to comply accordingly. Therefore, we must comply. The measure specified in Joint Announcement No. 1268, which requires merchants importing diesel to guarantee that it will not be used for refining kerosene, is hereby abolished. All merchants are to be informed accordingly. This announcement is made.

Amendment to Cargo Warehouse Regulations:

The government has now ordered that Article 18 of the regulations for general cargo warehouses be amended as follows: Article 18. Merchants who wish to remove goods from the warehouse for export overseas must first submit a declaration for the removal of goods for export, along with a guarantee that, should any irregularities occur, they will pay a sum no more than ten times the assessed tax amount within the period specified by Customs. Only after Customs verifies that the declaration matches the goods will a permit for the removal of goods for export be issued, and the goods released. If, after obtaining the permit and removing the goods from the warehouse, the merchant fails to ship all or part of the goods on the designated vessel, Customs may enforce the guarantee and require the merchant to pay the taxes due on the goods as stated in the permit. If Customs discovers, during loading, that all or part of the goods do not match the goods stated in the permit, or if the goods have been loaded and shipped but are unloaded privately in other parts of China with the intention of evasion, Customs may enforce the guarantee for the full amount. Merchants who wish to remove goods from the warehouse for bonded transport to other treaty ports must first submit a declaration for the removal of goods for bonded transport to other treaty ports, along with a guarantee that, if the goods are not declared for import at the Customs of the designated port following established procedures, the merchant will pay the import duties. Only after Customs verifies that the declaration matches the warehouse records will a permit for the removal of goods for bonded transport to other treaty ports be issued, and the goods released. If, after obtaining the permit and removing the goods from the warehouse, the merchant fails to ship the goods on the designated vessel as specified in the permit, Customs may act according to the guarantee. As for shut-out cargo, whether originally declared for export overseas or to other treaty ports, merchants may take delivery of the goods after paying import duties or return the goods to the Customs warehouse, as they see fit. However, the 12-month storage period will still be calculated from the date of the initial entry into the warehouse. These measures regarding the issuance of guarantees and the shipment of goods will take effect on March 1, 1934, and all goods removed from Customs warehouses from that date onward must be handled in accordance with these measures. All merchants are to be informed accordingly. This announcement is made.

People’s, Zhongnan, and 24 Other Cigarette Manufacturers Request Change in Tax Rates 124

Because Second-Level Tax Treatment of Chinese and Foreign Businesses is Extremely Unequal

Petition to the Executive Yuan and Legislative Yuan for Relief

Since the Ministry of Finance ordered the adoption of a two-tier cigarette tax system, with a tax rate of 120% for lower-grade cigarettes and 36% for higher-grade cigarettes, Chinese businesses, with their smaller capital, mostly deal in lower-grade cigarettes, putting them at a disadvantage, making it difficult to operate and maintain their business. Now, 24 cigarette manufacturers, including People's and Zhongnan, have jointly petitioned the Legislative Yuan, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Industry, and the Tax Bureau to request a change in the tax rate to protect Chinese manufacturers. The following is an excerpt from their petition: Petition to request that the current cigarette tax rate, which is unfair to Chinese and foreign businesses, be promptly revised to provide relief. (Omission)

Cigarette Consolidated Tax

was initiated in 1929. In November 1930, February 1931, and March 1932, the tax was revised three times. From July 1929 to November 1930, there was a seven-tier tax system; from November 1930 to February 1931, there was an old three-tier tax system; from February 1931 to March 1932, there was a new three-tier tax system; and from March 1932 to the present, there has been a two-tier tax system. (Omission) If the tax rate is divided into more tiers, the burden of the upper, middle, and lower taxes will vary in proportion to the quality of the cigarettes, so the burden of lower-grade cigarettes is lighter, giving Chinese businesses an advantageous position, and domestic tobacco leaves also sell well. If the tax rate is divided into fewer tiers, the burden of the upper, middle, and lower grades of cigarettes will not be very different, or even the burden of lower-grade cigarettes may exceed that of upper and middle-grade cigarettes by one or two parts, so the burden of upper and middle-grade cigarettes is lighter, giving British and American businesses an advantageous position, and domestic tobacco leaves also become difficult to sell. According to past experience, the seven-tier tax is most beneficial to Chinese businesses, followed by the three-tier tax, while the two-tier tax clearly gives special privileges to British and American businesses, leaving Chinese businesses with no power to resist. Therefore, during the seven-tier tax era, there were a total of 156 Chinese businesses. After the implementation of the two-tier tax, the increase was still 410,000, but now it has increased to one and decreased to 170,000. This is the result of reducing taxes on upper-grade cigarettes and increasing taxes on lower-grade cigarettes. As a result, the burden on British and American businesses has been sharply reduced, while the burden on Chinese businesses has doubled. No wonder that in one year, British and American businesses have made rapid progress, while the bankruptcies of Chinese businesses have accounted for almost two-thirds of the total. It cannot be said that the tax rate is not bad, benefiting British and American businesses at the expense of Chinese businesses. Is this something that the government, which cares for industry and Chinese businesses, would willingly do? Perhaps the advantages and disadvantages of this matter are not yet clear. (Omission)

The result of this year's tax change

is that the tax on lower-grade cigarettes has increased from 90% to more than 120%, while the tax on upper-grade cigarettes has decreased from 47% to 36%. Those who can afford to smoke cigarettes costing 300 yuan per case are wealthy merchants and magnates who have the ability to pay taxes and should bear a heavier burden. Those who smoke cigarettes costing 120 yuan per case are poor and humble people who lack the ability to pay taxes and should bear a lighter burden. (Omission) It may be said that the tax of 160 yuan collected on cigarettes above 300 yuan under the first-tier tax is not heavy. However, the sales of cigarettes above 300 yuan are extremely rare, and the 20 yuan allowance allowed outside the place of manufacture is almost equal to zero. In essence, the first-tier tax is just a decoration of the tax system, and only the second-tier tax is actually implemented, with cigarettes around 300 yuan only collecting 36%. (Omission) The tobacco leaves used in the lower and middle-grade cigarettes produced by Chinese businesses are produced in Henan, Shandong, and Anhui, or American tobacco leaves, or domestic tobacco leaves from Huanggang, Junzhou, Deng, Susong, and Xinchang. The annual output of American and domestic tobacco leaves is about 150 million pounds, with an average selling price of 20 cents per pound, and farmers earn about 30 million yuan annually. The government's flue-cured tobacco tax is 4 yuan and 15 cents per 100 catties, with a tax revenue of about 4.5 million yuan. The annual output of domestic tobacco leaves from Huanggang and Junzhou is about 100 million pounds, and the income of the government and farmers is worth one-third of the American and domestic tobacco leaves. During the seven-tier tax era, the tax rate and the value of the cigarettes were mutually standardized, so domestic tobacco leaves sold best. When the three-tier tax system was changed, the tax on upper-grade cigarettes was cheap, and the tax on lower-grade cigarettes was expensive, so the sales of American leaves

Collapsed one after another.

Now there are only 30 to 40 left, and in recent years the sales have decreased sharply and many have suffered losses. At the beginning of the two-tier tax system in 1932, merchants and people from all over the world opposed it, knowing that the treatment was unfair and that they were unable to compete with the British and Americans. (Omission) First, let's talk about the consumption of stamps. According to the regulations of the consolidated tax, every 50,000 cigarettes is a large case, and one stamp is affixed. The number of stamps consumed is the number of cases of cigarettes sold. During the three-tier tax era, the average number of British and American companies was 30,472, and the average number of other companies was 68,422. The number of British and American cigarettes sold was only 40% of the other companies, less than 50%. During the two-tier tax era, the average number of British and American companies was 48,808, and the average number of other companies was 44,323. The number of British and American cigarettes sold exceeded the other companies by 4,485. Alas, in one year, British and American companies have made such rapid progress, and Chinese businesses have declined so much. Those who have a heart cannot fail to lose their color and courage when they hear about it. Next, let's talk about

Tax payments.

During the three-tier tax era, the average number of British and American tobacco companies was 2,417,403.822, and the average number of other tobacco companies was 2,006,252.647. The burden of British and American companies was 410,000 more than that of Chinese businesses. During the two-tier tax era, the average number of British and American tobacco companies was 2,726,392.522, and the average number of other tobacco companies was 2,554,466.996. The burden of British and American companies was only 170,000 more than that of Chinese businesses. Comparing these two tables, during the three-tier tax era, although the sales of British and American companies were less than 50% of those of Chinese businesses, the amount of taxes paid each month was 410,000 more than that of Chinese businesses. The reason is that the quality of the cigarettes is good, and the selling price is high, so the tax is also high, which is very reasonable. Now that it has been changed to a two-tier tax, the number of British and American cigarettes sold, which was less than 50% of that of Chinese businesses, has increased to one. If the tax rate is fair, the amount of taxes paid by British and American companies should be at least doubled compared to Chinese businesses, but the fact is that it is only 170,000 more each month. The former sales were less than 50%, and the monthly tax payment

Took away domestic products.

Half of the tobacco leaves, last year the consolidated tax was changed to two-tier, and lower-grade cigarettes became even more difficult to establish themselves, so domestic tobacco leaves from Huanggang and Junzhou were not sold at all. This year, compared with last year, the tobacco leaves from Xuzhou, Weixian, and Fengyang were high in price and cheap in price, but there were fewer buyers, which was also affected by the heavy tax on lower-grade cigarettes. The prosperity and decline of lower-grade cigarettes are closely related to the sales of domestic tobacco leaves. If lower-grade cigarettes disappear from the market due to heavy taxes, the sales of domestic tobacco leaves will be cut off immediately. Not only will the government's tobacco tax suffer a great loss, but the rural areas will also go bankrupt as a result. Therefore, heavy taxation of lower-grade cigarettes is tantamount to suffocating the source of tax, directly harming Chinese businesses, and indirectly harming tobacco farmers. At this time of rural bankruptcy and rampant bandits, can the government not consider the millions of tobacco farmers and bear to put them in this dead place and drive fish into the abyss? (Omission) Urgent words, I hope to be adopted. In addition to being submitted separately, it is respectfully submitted to the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Industry, the Ministry of Finance, and the Tax Bureau, which are presented by the cigarette companies of the people, the Yoli cigarette factory, the Yonghe tobacco company, the China Dada cigarette factory, the Jiuyi cigarette company, the Jinshan cigarette factory, the Huafu cigarette factory, the Changming tobacco company, the Delong cigarette factory, the China Huaxing cigarette company, the Asia tobacco company, the Yuxin cigarette factory, the Xinmin cigarette factory, Huamei Tobacco Co., Ltd., Huaqing Tobacco Company, Jinsha Taiji Tobacco Company, Shanghai China Pacific Tobacco Company, Shanghai Tobacco Company, China Greater Southeast Ocean Tobacco Company, Zhongnan Cigarette Factory, Kefu Cigarette Company, Jiangsu and Zhejiang Cigarette Company, Hexing Cigarette Factory, Zhonghe Cigarette Company.

National Medical Association Submits to Ministry of Interior to Train Old-Style Midwives 125

The National Medical Association believes that the responsibilities of midwives are significant. Although the authorities have promulgated the "Midwives Ordinance," they have not strictly enforced it in the five years since, resulting in occasional transgressions. Old-style midwives continue to run rampant everywhere. Yesterday, the Association specially submitted a document to the Ministry of Interior requesting that local health authorities strictly enforce the law, stating: "Submitting this document to request the Ministry of Interior to order local health authorities to strictly enforce the Midwives Ordinance and train old-style midwives in order to value human lives. It is believed that midwives hold the lives of both mothers and infants in their hands, with the power of life and death. Their responsibilities are of utmost importance. Therefore, all advanced countries in the East and West have specially enacted ordinances to manage them with utmost rigor. In the past, even the Beijing government, amidst its deep-rooted bad habits and political decay, recognized the importance of this matter and promulgated the "Registration of Midwives and Training of Midwives Ordinance," which was deemed appropriate by knowledgeable individuals. Our National Government, at the beginning of its tutelage, was determined to revitalize the country. The "Examination Rules for Midwives" were promulgated earlier, followed by the "Midwives Ordinance," demonstrating the authorities' concern for the people's well-being. However, for the past five years, midwives in various regions have inevitably committed transgressions, and old-style birth attendants continue to run rampant everywhere, with no end in sight. This is likely due to the failure of local health authorities to effectively enforce the laws. The Association is alarmed and distressed and unable to provide remedies. It is deeply concerned that if this continues, it will become increasingly difficult to rectify the situation. Therefore, the Second Congress of Representatives resolved to request the Ministry to actively supervise local health authorities to strictly enforce the Midwives Ordinance, while also initiating the training of old-style midwives to strive for a safe transition between the old and new systems. We hereby submit ten articles of advice on the general principles of midwife training for your review and implementation. We await your command with utmost anticipation. Respectfully submitted to the Ministry of Interior, with attached advice on the general principles of midwife training: (1) Name: Midwife Training Center of a certain city or county. (2) Purpose: To teach the essential points and methods of midwifery, so that old-style midwives who have been engaged in midwifery can learn the points to pay attention to during childbirth. (3) Qualifications: Old-style midwives who have been recognized by the police station or public security bureau will be compelled to study by the health authorities. Those who disobey will be prohibited from operating. (4) Duration: Three months, twice a week, for at least two hours each time. The time will be determined by the training center. (5) Subjects: Outline of human anatomy and physiology, methods of fetal position diagnosis, methods of perineal protection, methods of umbilical cord ligation, disinfection methods, emergency methods, fetal resuscitation methods, with an emphasis on practical exercises. Use illustrations and models to demonstrate. Use oral instruction without handouts. (6) Enrollment: Each class will be limited to 50 students. If the number exceeds the limit, two classes will be set up. (7) Location and faculty: The health authorities will entrust official or public or equivalent private hospitals, and the faculty will be concurrently staffed by the staff of those hospitals, all on a voluntary basis. (8) Tuition: Entirely free. (9) Graduation: Those who attend all sessions and pass the oral examination will be given a certificate. Those who fail will be ordered to enter the second class to continue listening. (10) Implementation: These general principles will be followed by the local

Health authorities to implement, and the progress and dates of commencement will be reported to the superior authorities for filing with the Ministry. The same will be done upon graduation.

Two Railways Improve North Station 126

Held North Station Station Affairs Meeting

Resolved Various Reform Cases

The Two Railways Bureau held three consecutive meetings in the Traffic Department meeting room to improve the Shanghai North Station's station operations. The attendees included Zheng Baozhao, Yuan Shaochang, Xie Wenlong, Wang Zhigang, Tang Huannan, Wang Shuchun, Sun Suizhi, Zou Quxin, Li Zhaoyu, Chen Guoliang, Jin Zhu, Liang Ying, Pu Zijun, Shi Debi, Ouyang Zhi, and Fu Mengxiong, a total of sixteen people. The chairman was Yuan Shaochang, and the recorder was Tang Xiongjie. The various motions passed are recorded as follows:

Director's Instructions

First, Zheng Baozhao, Director of the Traffic Department, delivered a speech, saying: "Shanghai is the commercial center of the country, ranking fourth among the world's major commercial ports. Chinese and foreigners live together, and its importance is evident. The North Station is also the hub of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways, with tens of thousands of Chinese and foreign passengers every day. Whether its management is appropriate or not has a significant impact on international reputation. Therefore, all facilities at the station must be improved at any time to meet the needs. This is the original intention of convening today's meeting. As for the key points of improvement, there are roughly two: (1) material improvement, such as the construction of station buildings and all other facilities in the station, etc.; (2) spiritual improvement, such as the diligence of employees, the speed of handling, and the harmony, integrity, etc. We should pay attention to both of these, and we should not allow any neglect, then the station affairs will progress day by day, which can be expected. If you want to seek any improvement in your career, it is impossible to succeed without gathering the strength of all and working together. Therefore, the colleagues at the North Station must be consistent from top to bottom, regardless of each other, and for the employees of other departments of this road and all relevant parties, such as the municipal government, security department, public security bureau, banking industry, hotel industry, automobile industry, and transportation industry, we should contact each other and assist each other. For the employees under their jurisdiction, it is necessary to be selfless, to take talents as the standard, and to treat everyone equally, without taking private friendship as a prerequisite. For passengers and merchants, regardless of rank, they should be treated kindly, whether they are wholesale or retail. All customers should be treated well. For superiors, they should follow the instructions of the Director to the section chiefs last time, breaking away from sentimentality, being honest and reliable, and not deceiving the old and young, and not discounting them. Check this record of instructions. It is necessary for all colleagues to read it, so it has been printed by this office and distributed to each section station. I hope that you can follow it at any time and contribute suggestions for improvement at any time."

Discussing the Motions

Discussing the motions, (1) All personnel at the information desk should wear uniforms uniformly. (Resolution) Uniforms have recently been approved and should be worn accordingly. (2) Set up a timetable wooden sign to make it easier for passengers to understand. (Resolution) The principle is approved. Liang Ying, the leading clerk of the information desk, Ouyang Zhi, the section clerk of the business section, and Wang Shuchun, the section chief of the car service section of the Su-Song section, should each submit a draft of the location, style, and size to the office for evaluation and approval. (3) Set up vending stalls and eliminate platform vendors. (Resolution) Platform vendors should be eliminated immediately. Vending stalls should be set up near the inspection station of the Public Security Bureau in the west of the station, and there is no need to set up more inside the station to maintain cleanliness. (4) Rectify the baggage carriers. (Resolution) (A) Station attendants and inspectors should train all carriers at any time. When transporting luggage, they must be careful to avoid damage. (B) If any carrier treats customers rudely, station attendants and inspectors will strictly investigate and deal with them. (C) If the current number of people is insufficient, the station attendants and inspectors should prepare a work distribution table and submit it to the office for verification. (D) The handling fee for transporting baggage with export tags should be collected by the carrier foreman next to the baggage scale, not by the baggage carriers from the passengers, to prevent extortion. The status quo should be maintained for imported baggage with tags and all baggage without tags. (5) The uniforms of the employees should be neat and clean to invigorate the spirit. (Resolution) The station affairs inspector should be responsible for supervision. (6) Time and direction signs for incoming trains should be added to the platform. (Resolution) This office has already verified it in another case and should not be discussed.

Ad Hoc Proposals

(1) All imported baggage should be picked up in the baggage room to avoid passengers gathering on the platform and hindering order. (Resolution) The principle is approved, but the baggage room is small and not

Sufficient for use and cannot be realized. (2) Install electric bells inside the platform so that those sending off can get off the bus in time. (Resolution) Ask the electrical engineer to evaluate the price before approving it. (3) The waiting room doors for the third and fourth class should be rebuilt to face south. (Resolution) The current direction is still appropriate and does not need to be rebuilt. (4) When a train arrives, a road police officer should stand at the end of the platform to prevent people from entering and exiting. (Resolution) Send a letter to the police station to do so. (5) The baggage handlers standing at the entrance should be arranged in order. (Resolution) Recommend Ouyang Zhi, a clerk of the business section, and Fu Mengxiong, a station affairs inspector, to discuss solutions together. (6) Stipulate the location of the disclosure sign. (Resolution) It is temporarily set on the wall opposite the ticket office, the stationmaster's office, and the dining room. (7) Suppress unlicensed vendors outside the station. (Resolution) Consult Mr. Li Yushu of the general affairs office to contact the Bureau of Works. (8) If there is a delay in the passenger car, the station manager should notify the information desk one hour in advance to answer passengers. (Resolution) Passed. The meeting adjourned.

Resolution of the Fatal Car Accident Case of Liu Rongtai on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway 127

The Railway Bureau Continues to Raise 767 Yuan in Compensation

To Gather a Total of 3,000 Yuan for the Bereaved Family of Liu

Xin Xin News Agency reports that on January 9th of the 20th year of the Republic [1931], Liu Rongtai, the president of the Zhabei Fire Brigade in Shanghai, set out to fight a fire. Due to reckless driving, he was hit by a Shanghai-Nanjing Railway train and died. His bereaved family's request for compensation remained unresolved for a long time. This year, Liu's wife, Liu Li, again sued the Railway Bureau in the Shanghai District Court, requesting a judgment for the Railway Bureau to compensate for losses of approximately 51,600 yuan. After the Railway Bureau entrusted consultant Zhang, a lawyer, to handle the defense, the court ruled that the Bureau should hand over the original collected compensation of 1,233 yuan to settle the case, as previously reported. Liu Li, dissatisfied, appealed to the Suzhou Higher Court. The court, considering the litigation between the two parties as a waste of litigation fees, advised reconciliation and instructed the Railway Bureau to continue raising 767 yuan in compensation to reach a total of 3,000 yuan. Both parties accepted this. Consultant Zhang, a lawyer, also requested that his court appearance fee of 200 yuan be donated to the compensation, it is said.

Continued Hearing of the Zhu Baoyuan Estate Case 128

Zhu Shunqing Fails to Appear in Court Due to Illness

Discrepancies Found in the Estate Inventory

Following the death of Zhu Baoyuan, owner of Zhenhe Tea Company, his second wife, Zhu Xi, and his two sons, Zhu Yanqing and Zhu Shunqing, became involved in a lawsuit in the First Special District Court over the division of the estate. Various hearings and summonses have been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Qiao Wanxuan continued the hearing. Zhu Shunqing, suffering from hemoptysis, was unable to appear in court, as evidenced by a prescription provided by his lawyer. Therefore, only the first defendant, Zhu Yanqing, appeared in court. Judge Qiao first inquired about the time of his father's death, then asked whether the estate inventory provided by the plaintiff was accurate, and presented the list for review. After reviewing, Yanqing stated that the amount was not that large. He then reported the property items one by one. Most of them matched the plaintiff's list, but there were also several items with discrepancies in the amount or that were completely absent. In addition, he declared that although the property existed, Zhu Baoyuan had decided to gift it to his two brothers before his death. The court then inquired about the Zhenhe Tea Company's account books. Yanqing replied that all account books from the previous year and the year before had been sent to accountant Xu for auditing. The accountant had already submitted a detailed report along with the account books. This year, because business had not yet concluded, the account books were still needed for daily use and therefore remained in the shop. However, as it had not been settled, the details could not be clearly stated. As for the plaintiff's claim about a handwritten property ledger of his father's, he had never seen it. His father only had a diary recording various properties, which had already been submitted in the previous case. There were no other handwritten records, he said. The plaintiff's lawyer then questioned Yanqing repeatedly about the fact that he had stated Zhenhe's annual turnover was several hundred thousand or over a million, while the declared capital was only twenty thousand. Yanqing replied that in Shanghai, many tea shops had a capital of only thirty to fifty thousand, while their annual turnover was several hundred thousand or millions. This was true not only for tea shops but also for other businesses. The lawyer then presented questions about the shop's business conditions, income and expenses, and personnel changes over the years, questioning the defendant for a long time. By five o'clock, Judge Qiao adjourned the hearing to a later date.

Intending to Abandon Her After Cohabitation

The Defendant Claims the Girl is a Prostitute

Hou Guohua, owner of Hua Kang Woolen Shop, is a native of Ningbo, nearing forty years old. He had been cohabitating with a woman surnamed Qi, appearing as husband and wife. Hou's goal was achieved, and he took it a step further and

Rented a House for Cohabitation

However, he always perfunctorily evaded Xiuying's urging for marriage, saying he needed to wait for the approval of his elders or that his fate was unfavorable. By last summer, Xiuying was pregnant, and he used the excuse of her large belly being unsightly, saying that he would perform the wedding ceremony after she gave birth. Before long, Xiuying discovered Hou's secret with the woman surnamed Qi, and she realized that Hou was a lecherous rogue who did not want to formally marry her to avoid interference from the Qi woman. So, she wrote to her mother, asking her to come to Shanghai to take charge. After Tang Wang arrived, Hou immediately asked his brother to intercede, promising to sever ties with the Qi woman and to marry her after she gave birth, and he was willing to designate 5,000 yuan as security, guaranteeing that he would not abandon her, and giving another 1,000 yuan as consolation money. Pretend it was Her Own Child

It was difficult to acknowledge, and his actions were bizarre. The Tang Wang mother and daughter were at a loss. Hou then invited his brother, the Qi woman, and several lawyers to swarm in, creating a threatening situation, forcing the Tang five mother and daughter to hand over the previously written agreement and the newborn child. Disrupted the Family

Enticed and abducted a girl under the age of twenty, taking her away from the guardianship of the person with parental rights, luring her to Shanghai with the intent of sexual intercourse. His actions constitute a crime under Article 257, Section 2 of the Criminal Code. Furthermore, he disrupted public morals by using deception to make the girl mistakenly believe that there was a spousal relationship, indulging his animalistic desires. His actions constitute a crime under Article 244, Section 1 of the same law. Finally, he damaged her reputation by publicly insulting her and attempting to abandon her in bad faith, violating his agreement. His actions constitute crimes under Articles 324 and 310 of the same law. He should be severely punished to deter evil and maintain public morals. They also attached a private prosecution, requesting that he be ordered to fulfill the agreement, it was said. Reading Q&A

Questions and Answers on Ancient Poetry 143

This column is a part of the "Reading Guidance" work and publishes general reading questions. As for research methods for various subjects, because the scope of the questions involved is too large, it is planned to compile introductions to self-study for various subjects separately, which will not be published in this column. Other questions such as reading difficulties and individual questions will be answered separately by letter. However, recent letters from readers have asked to publish more concrete reading questions. In order to have more academic discussions, the department is also willing to publish the questions that are of an academic nature and are needed by general readers after consideration. Here, the department's specially appointed special committee member, Mr. Shen Xinqing, answers several questions about ancient poetry asked by Mr. Liu Qiushi for readers' research. Editor's note.

Reading Guidance:

I am currently studying poetry, and there are several points that I do not understand, so I am writing to ask.

(1) Does ancient poetry have metrical rules?

(2) How many kinds of changes have there been in ancient poetry from ancient times to the present?

(3) What kind of metrical rules are the standard for ancient poetry?

(4) Is there a limit to the sound and melody of ancient poetry?

Sincerely, Liu Qiushi

Reply to Mr. Liu Qiushi

(1) Ancient poetry has the distinction of four-character, five-character, seven-character, and long and short sentences; the Han Yuefu also has three-character ones.

(2) The changes of ancient poetry generally go from four-character to five-character, and from five-character to seven-character. Long and short sentences are changes of seven-character sentences.

(3) In addition to the two points mentioned above, there is no so-called standard; however, four-character sentences take the Book of Songs as the ancestor, and its style is the oldest.

(4) The rhythm of ancient poetry is magical and clear, and depends on the individual, without limit. Read more and write more, and you will gradually enter a better state. As for phonology, it is another specialized field of study and cannot be limited to writing poetry.

(Mail Delivery) Mr. Tian Hualong, Nanjing: Please indicate the mailing address for a reply by letter.

(Mail Delivery 2) He Benzhi and Zhou Kaifang, Hankou: Your letter has been received. I am sorry that I cannot answer your questions, because they are outside the scope of this section.

Chunqiu (Annals)

Explanation of "January 28th" 147

— Nineteen

Time passes easily, and the terrible "January 28th" has resurfaced before our—we Chinese—eyes! Mr. Wang Rongfu of the Qing Dynasty had three essays titled "Explanation of San Jiu" (Explanation of Three Nines), in which he explained the numbers from one to nine very thoroughly. Based on his theory, I wrote "Explanation of One Two Eight."

In "Explanation of San Jiu I," Mr. Wang said at the beginning, "One is odd, two is even, one and two cannot be counted as a number"; that is, the two characters "one" and "two" are already very empty. He also said, "Nine is the completion of numbers"; then "eight" is not a completed number either. Based on this explanation, how much of the impression of "January 28th" still remains in the minds of people across the country today? Although it seems that it cannot be measured accurately, since these three characters are not completed numbers, then the so-called "January 28th" is probably just a flash in the pan in newspapers, slogans, or oral presentations: The result: I am afraid that it will disappear with the bullet marks and artillery traces of Songhu. Is this not a very sad thing!

Try to break down the three characters "January 28th" again, and take any two characters to add together. Strangely, the result cannot give us a satisfactory answer. For example, adding one and two results in "three". Mr. Wang said: "Three is the completion of numbers". To put it badly, this word "completion" means that the fact has been established, and there is no need to say it again. Adding one and eight results in "nine". Mr. Wang defines this word "nine" as "the end of numbers". He also said: "Nine is an imaginary number". Therefore, the word "nine" is also very empty; and it may even come to an end here. And Mr. Wang also said: "If three cannot be exhausted, then it is about nine to show that it is much more, this is the imaginary number of language." Therefore, no matter whether one and eight or one and two are added together, it always hits a wall, but only becomes an "imaginary number" in language. Then what about adding two and eight? Adding two and eight results in "ten". However, Mr. Wang said, "Accumulating to ten is to return to one," so "ten cannot be counted as a number"; then it is another empty sign. Try adding the three characters "January 28th" together. The result happens to be "eleven". Since "ten" cannot be counted as a number, and "one" cannot be counted as a number, isn't this another big emptiness?

In short, the tricky and weird three characters "January 28th" are calculated back and forth, and they always give you bad luck, with no chance to succeed; then, you might as well say that this is the destiny of the Chinese people. I wonder how the "upper" and "lower" classes of the whole country feel about this?

Silly 148

— Chunliu

Since I was a child, I have been recognized by most people as being a bit "silly." Although I once spent a night reading half of the Book of Songs in the private school; and when I was eleven years old, the teacher asked me to write a four-rhyme "Fu-De Poem," but I doubled my efforts and wrote eight rhymes. However, because of this, people generally said that I was silly, and Mr. Liu, who taught me the longest, added another word and called me silly.

In fact, when it comes to "silly," the word "silly" is different from words like "dull" and "stupid" in terms of its meaning, and it has a subtle meaning of its own. Why should I not be a fool?

Thinking about it carefully: Which great inventors in the world do not have a bit of silliness? May I ask, lying well on the ground, seeing an apple fall to the ground, you have to think of the earth's gravity; standing next to a stove, seeing the lid move, you have to think of something about the effect of steam; obviously living in the quite comfortable ancient civilized capital, suddenly thinking that there will be a vacant lot on the other side of the water; to test the induction of radio, tying a copper wire kite and letting it go to the sky, are these inventors silly enough?

Because they are a bit silly, they can firmly stick to their beliefs, and the ideals that are radiated from a certain belief are true ideals. As the Western saying goes, "The ideal is the mother of fact," we can say: "Silliness is the mother of ideals, and thus the grandmother of facts."

Why should I not be a fool? I'm just afraid that I'm not qualified enough to be a fool!

Four Characteristics of the Capital 149

— Yiqiu

Last year in Wuxi, I remember writing an article called "Four Characteristics," which occupied a corner of this column. That was about the characteristics of Wuxi. Now I feel that Nanjing has more differences from other places, and the capital, which is the capital of the country, must have its own characteristics, so I write four characteristics again:

"Many government offices": The capital is also our national capital. How can the national capital be anything if there are not many government offices? Therefore, our capital has a particularly large number of government offices, especially in the northern part of the city. No matter on the streets or in the alleys, there are government offices everywhere. In terms of political affairs, from the district office straight to the National Government. In terms of party affairs, from the district branch straight to the central party headquarters. In terms of military affairs, from the company straight to the Military Commission. All levels are complete, plus various committees and parallel agencies, which are truly magnificent and extremely solemn. Many schools or printing factories, as long as they are established by the government, must have soldiers or police standing guard at the door.

"Many officials": With many government offices, there are certainly many officials. All political officials, party officials, military officers, etc., from sesame green bean officials to the Chairman of the National Government, members of the Central Committee, or military giants, all levels are complete. Therefore, officials with briefcases under their arms and badges on their chests can be seen everywhere. Especially in front of the Confucius Temple on Sundays, you can simply bump into badge comrades everywhere. The singing girl's book societies and various entertainment venues rely on them to survive, which is truly a great merit.

"Many singing girls": Because there are many officials, there are also many singing girls. These women who sell smiles for a living decorate their appearance neatly one by one to provide entertainment for others every time the evening lights come on. On the surface, it is indeed selling art, but what is the value of just one "art" in China? Therefore, in order to maintain their survival, they have to sell their bodies as well. The old men of the book societies pay them very little, only a few dimes a day, which is not enough for them to pay for a meal, so their lives depend entirely on ordering plays, and those customers, how can they not have other intentions when they come to order your play? Ah! Those fallen and unfortunate women, when I passed by the Qinhuai River and heard their sad melodies squeezed out for a bowl of rice, it will surely arouse my infinite feelings of drama and dismay!

"Many beggars": Because there are many government offices, many officials, and many singing girls, and the result of the lack of production agencies - factories - has created the current situation of many beggars, which is truly a hidden worry for society. Here, no matter in bustling cities or remote alleys, there are beggars everywhere. In recent days, the weather has been severely cold, and a group of old and young beggars with scant clothing are begging from door to door, from morning to dusk, in a continuous stream. The store residents feel that it is very annoying, but if you think about it from the beggars' point of view, the weather is freezing cold, the number of beggars has suddenly increased, and it is difficult to get enough to eat even if you beg all day, which is also very pitiful. I hope that the ruling gentlemen will quickly find a fundamental solution for relief.

Frozen Corpses on the Road 151

— Zikang

The freezing wind blew like a sharp blade on the morning road; I pulled up my collar, and shrank

to pass through a remote alley. Beside the alley entrance on the right, many people were gathered, watching the spectacle. Driven by curiosity, I also stepped forward a couple of paces to see what was happening.

It turned out that in the midst of the crowd, an elderly, dying beggar was lying on the ground. On his face, exposed beyond the many layers of rice straw covering his body, his eyes were already tightly shut, but some of his muscles seemed to still be twitching, and every so often, three shallow breaths escaped him. At that moment, a kind-hearted woman came from within the alley, placing some silver ingots and the like beside him, followed by lighting some incense sticks.

I asked a middle-aged man next to me: "Why not send him to the hospital?"

"What hope is there? --He's as good as dead!"

People had already declared him as good as dead; and they had already left some silver ingots and lit incense sticks for him, so what else was there to say? Thus, I was forced to run away wordlessly, carrying my sorrowful heart!

Chapter 23: Unbearable Pain, Listening Intently to Festive Music; Joy Not Yet Satisfied, Hastened Departure Upon Receiving an Urgent Message

Ji Zhi said: Just wait another day or two. Madam Gan smiled and said, according to your brother's wishes:

, he wanted you to return to school long ago, but I said to wait until after today. Ji Zhi casually asked: Why wait until after today? Madam Gan said: The reason is very simple, isn't it to let you attend today's wedding feast? Ji Zhi said: Ah! You

are talking about the happy event across the street. I have no dealings with the Zhao family. Madam Gan said: That's really strange. According to custom, all neighbors should receive an invitation, especially since you know both the bride and groom. They shouldn't have forgotten you. The annoying military music grew louder, followed by a long string of firecrackers and the cheerful cheers of many people, lasting for a full two hours. Ji Zhi was usually too lazy to listen to such sounds, but he didn't understand why he didn't want to hide in the backyard to avoid them, nor did he want to open his books to distract himself. He just sat blankly in the room, listening to the sounds. After about an hour, the boisterous music could still be faintly heard over several walls. From this, he knew that the Zhao and Yang families had many guests. He further imagined how happy Guizhi and Zhao Ziqiang must be, while he was unlucky enough to return to Haidian and hear this happiness. He thought depressively for a long time and couldn't bear it any longer. He finally went to the upper room to talk with his brother and sister-in-law, to escape the sounds. In the evening, as he lay in bed, he thought, I will completely put these irrelevant matters aside. As my brother said, tomorrow I will return to Dahongmen to teach. (231)
