Film Special

An Interview with Chinese Film Artists (35) (Continued from the 22nd of This Month) 230

— Sha Ji

(15) "Roar, China!" Director Ying Yunwei (Part 1)

If we think 1933 is worth remembering, then "Roar, China!," which premiered at the Golden Theater, will never disappear from our memory. Now, this director has moved from the stage to the screen. Because he is a noteworthy figure, I interviewed him at Yi Hua Company.

Sitting next to the stove, I asked him to talk to us.

"What do you want me to say?" he said. "I don't have any film works out yet, which makes it very difficult for me."

"I don't think it matters. Your work will be seen by us in the near future anyway. Please tell us about your journey from the stage to the screen."

"The transition from stage to screen is a very ordinary phenomenon. There is nothing particularly worth mentioning for me. In fact, my interest in stage plays comes entirely from film. Because I work in the shipping industry, I haven't had the opportunity to enter the film industry for ten years, so I had to engage in stage play experiments in my spare time. From "The Merchant of Venice" to last year's "Roar, China!," I have gained a lot of experience in drama. However, amateur drama, due to various reasons, cannot give us better results, because from the director to the stagehands, everyone is an amateur trying. At the same time, one performance cannot last more than a week, and the rent for the stage is expensive, which is not a condition for reducing seat prices and extending the dates. Therefore, people from other places cannot come to see the play, and most audiences cannot afford the high ticket prices, so it is not widespread. Therefore, one performance takes a lot of effort, but the effect is not as great as that of film. In addition, I have recently felt deeply that the shipping industry cannot allow me to develop. Instead of trying to do drama in my spare time, it is better to engage in film directly. Needless to say, in film, as long as you work hard once, it can be screened everywhere and exist forever. This is my motivation for joining Yi Hua."

"Can you briefly talk about the relationship between stage plays and film, sir?" I asked.

(To be continued)

Film Review

Review of "Berkeley Square" 231

— Ling He

|Produced by Fox. Premiered at Cathay|

After watching the large-scale production of "Cavalcade," we will not immediately forget the name of the director Frank Lloyd. Now he has released "Berkeley Square." He is British. In the silent film era, he made famous films such as "The Woman Disputed." These works were well-received in the United States in the past, especially "The Woman Disputed" and "The Voice of the City," which were recognized as his masterpieces. By the sound film era, some people believed that Love Romance-style works were not his forte. As for so-called masterpieces, they were even more impossible to reproduce.

When "Cavalcade" premiered in Shanghai, we were probably all very impressed with his archaeological spirit and the large scenes and sets that did not spare wages. However, in terms of the overall work, it is inevitably too focused on the development of the story, that is, the "story-driven" film as we say. In particular, it is depressing, obscure, and unwelcome to the general audience. Of course, we do not deny that he handled every scene of the play very meticulously and thoughtfully, but the story is too long, and the general audience cannot savor the dialogue, so he only ended up with a result of putting in a lot of effort but not being appreciated.

Now let's look at this so-called "Berkeley Square." His style is still the same as "Cavalcade," slow pace, quiet atmosphere, extremely boiling but suppressed emotions, melancholic and long sadness, delicate tenderness. These are undoubtedly the strengths of romanticism, and for the intellectual class, they are deeply moved by it.

Naturally, this extreme sentiment is not a good thing for young people who are striving to make progress, especially for young people who are worn down by reality, who will be subjected to a kind of bad anesthesia. We don't have to intuitively criticize the absurdity of the immortality of the soul, because we have long recognized that famous works similar to "The Sorrows of Young Werther" are definitely not good tonics for modern times; moreover, seeking a conclusion of love-supremacism in the immortality of the soul.

Of course, we will definitely not turn a deaf ear to the playwright's cursing of reality, so that the negative expression of worries about the current society, when Stanley, in the capacity of a person from another world, tells the dead of the eighteenth century about the civilization of the present world. But how cowardly and ridiculous is this!

As for the purpose of the play explained in the manual, it is simply the opposite of the film. Is this "Berkeley Square" really doing a counter-article? We believe that this kind of explanation cannot reverse the mistake of the work.

As mentioned earlier, if we only use the eyes of an appreciator and purely objectively accept this poetic technique, people with rich emotions and fascinated by old-fashioned art will definitely feel a certain degree of satisfaction. However, if we take critical learning as the principle, we can affirm that this is dead art, relics in the tomb. Moreover, there is no reason for non-subjective existence at all. For anything, it must be an objective fact, plus a subjective understanding. Leaving one's own standpoint and becoming a purely objective prisoner is ultimately not the attitude we should adopt.

After watching this film, we immediately recall Norma Shearer's "Smilin' Through," and even more remind us of Leslie Howard in that film. His amorous son's demeanor in "Smilin' Through" is once again taught to us in this film. This is probably his own personality. Whether in "The Green Hat" or "Secrets," he still performs with the same style of music analysis. As for that English girl who plays Helen Angel, although we rarely meet, she teaches people to keep a lovely impression. Isn't it easy to give people a good impression with that dignified, quiet, and affectionate posture?

The United Photoplay Service Second Studio's Autograph Book 232

Recently, it has become popular in the United Photoplay Service Second Studio to place an autograph book and ask colleagues and friends to sign it to keep as a souvenir. The first was Wu Cun, the director of "Wind," followed by Cai Chusheng, the director of "Song of the Fishermen," actors Wang Renmei, Li Lili, and recently Sun Yu, the director of "Sports Queen," also made a book. Wu Cun's book is the most petite and exquisite, just like him; Cai Chusheng's book is the largest and most luxurious; Wang Renmei's book is almost the same; Li Lili's book is neither big nor small, just right to put in a pocket; Sun Yu's book is very simple and the price is the cheapest, because he always holds a simple doctrine, although a few dollars to buy an autograph book is no problem for him, but he always thinks that as long as the motive is sincere, there is no need to pay attention to the beauty of the paper and the sophistication of the binding. Among the several books, Wang Renmei and Li Lili's are almost full, Sun Yu's has only a few pages written on because it was recently made. Recently, Han Langen also has a book, but his book is an old-fashioned Chinese account book, even simpler than Sun Yu's. However, when he holds it with both hands and asks his colleagues to sign it, those who don't know it really think he is urging them to pay their debts?

"Pear Blossoms in a Rainstorm" to Be Completed in a Few Days 233

At the United Photoplay Service First Studio, under the efforts of the staff, Ma-Xu Weibang's new film "Pear Blossoms in a Rainstorm" has only one factory scene left to shoot. Because this scene is very large, and the studio is rushing to produce this film, the old and new photography studios are full of sets for this play, so this scene is built at the United Photoplay Service Second Studio. Now, the various scenes set up at the First Studio have been gradually completed, and the factory scene set up at the Second Studio is being rushed to be built by the set designer Wu Yonggang. It will be able to start shooting in a few days. When the shooting of this scene is completed, the whole play will be successfully completed. According to reports, this play is written and directed by Ma-Xu Weibang himself and is his first work after joining the United Photoplay Service. The leading actors are Gao Zhanfei, Chen Yanyan, Tan Ying, and He Feiguang, several major stars.

Tianyi News 234

Chen Yumei in New Clothes Chen Yumei always wears cloth when buying new clothes in order to promote thrift. This does not seem to have anything new to offer, but under her ingenious conception, these cloth-made new clothes want to surpass any clothes made of precious materials. Recently, she used blue homespun cloth to make a cheongsam in a new style, matched with her graceful figure, which is really elegant. Now, Ye Qiuxin, Chen Chili, Wang Huijuan, etc., are all imitating this style of clothing, and this new outfit has become popular in Tianyi.

The Basketball Team's New Uniforms The Tianyi Basketball Team is divided into men's and women's teams. The men's team is hosted by Tang Xiaodan, and the women's team is hosted by Chen Yumei. Recently, Li Yingguan Wenda, etc., have joined the men's team, and Fan Xuepeng Lu Jianfen have joined the women's team. It is said that Chen Yumei, etc., plan to take advantage of the fact that "Happy Enemies" has not yet started shooting to schedule a match with the men's team to determine the winner. Because the original uniforms are not suitable for winter wear, new winter uniforms will be made for the men's and women's players to wear.

Interesting People and Things 235

— Cun Nong

(1)

The weight of Bu Wancang, the director of "Golden Age," is extraordinary. Yesterday, in the director's room, he was discussing the script of "Woman" with Shi Dongshan. Director Bu conveniently sat down on a chair. Probably because he used too much force, with a loud "crack," one of the legs of the chair broke off. Fortunately, Lao Bu was clever and jumped up quickly, so he didn't fall. However, the people in the director's room all laughed.

(2)

Things turned out unexpectedly. This time, the Chinese team succumbed to the Jewish team, and countless fans could not help but feel very depressed, but in the film industry, a cinematographer was happy. Who is this person? Namely, Zhou Ke, a cinematographer from Yi Hua Company. Because Zhou Ke has the nickname of a Jewish millionaire, many people said to him: "Jewish millionaire, I didn't expect your country to be so powerful this year"! Zhou Ke listened and had a complacent look on his face, repeatedly saying: "If I hadn't come out, it would have been even more victorious"! At that time, it aroused great laughter.

(3)

It's really strange. Everyone calls Yue Feng "Mr. Ichiboku Saburo" when they see him. The reason is that at the Yi Hua Company's get-together, Yue Feng and Wang Yin performed selling medicine. Yue Feng played a Japanese person, and this Japanese person's name was "Ichiboku Saburo." Therefore, Yue Feng has the nickname "Ichiboku Saburo." At the same time, Yue Feng is even shorter, which is quite in line with the nickname "Ichiboku Saburo," but Yue Feng often says "I dare not, I dare not."

"Where to Settle Down" to Be Screened in Beijing Tomorrow 236

"Where to Settle Down," distributed by the Great Light Film Company, stars Huang Manli, Lu Yan, Wei Guangshou, He Zhigang, etc. The purpose of the whole play is to focus on social trends, and the consciousness is very commendable. The director has even more surpassing skills in this film, and there are many small movements. Huang Manli plays Xuefen in the film, and her performance is incomparably sad, which can be said to be her most outstanding work. This film will be screened at the Beijing Grand Theater starting tomorrow (Sunday).

Film Novel

Broadway Thru a Keyhole (7) 237

— Xin Zhi

Clark said, "I'm not afraid of anything as long as you love me." Joan Hyland said, "But you don't know who Frank Lock is. He'll be here any minute now." Before she could finish, someone was already knocking on the door. Joan ran to the door and opened it a crack. Lock asked, "Are you dressed yet?" Joan hid behind the door and whispered, "No, no, not yet." Lock said with an icy face, "Then what's that singer doing in your room?" After he said that, he stuck one foot in the door and pushed it open. Joan desperately wanted to protect Clark, but Clark had already walked up to Lock. Lock said to Joan for the first time in an angry voice, "Get out!" Joan pleaded, "I asked him to come. Please don't blame him." But Lock narrowed his eyes into a small slit, revealing a fierce light inside. He grabbed Joan's hand and threw her out the side door. Then, with a bang, he closed the door.

At this critical moment, Clark calmly stared at Lock. This was a test of his courage. Even when Lock reached into his pocket, he remained unchanged. He said, "Lock, I didn't expect to meet you like this. I wanted to see you about Joan." Lock still showed an unpredictable attitude, waiting for Clark to continue. Clark said, "Now that we've met, I don't know where to start. I've heard people say you're very fair." Clark paused, knowing that what he was about to say might cost him his life. He said, "I know I love her more than I love my own life. If I can't get her in the end, I'm willing to face whatever happens. You can either have people beat me to death, or you can do it yourself, but you can't stop me from loving her." At this time, Clark's words poured out of his mouth: "Mr. Lock, I can't believe I'm standing here talking to you. I'm not someone who's afraid to die. But I don't have that one thing in the world, that thing that gives me the courage to stand in front of you and tell you the truth from my heart, and I can't live." He swallowed some saliva and said, "Joan has told me how much you've helped her. She is endlessly grateful to you, but you can't confuse gratitude with love. The reason I came here this time is not because she asked me to come - she doesn't want you to know I'm here - because she's afraid you'll be against me. I'm very lucky to be able to meet you today, so I can tell you how sincerely I love her. I want to marry her. Lock, it's all up to you. Please decide whether to let me die or let me live."

Lock put down his cigarette. He slowly walked up to Clark. He looked at Clark for a while and slowly said, "Okay, take good care of her." After he said that, he took his hat and gloves and left. A few weeks later, everyone in the vaudeville industry of Broadway and the big shots on Park Street all knew about the wedding of a nightclub star and a famous singer, and the president of the Manhattan Chicken and Duck Protection Association, Frank Lock, also wore a formal dress and a top hat, squeezed among the gentlemen watching the ceremony. (To be continued)
